Shen Bao Architectural Weekly

When Building Public Housing (Continued)

— Xi Hao

...Several points to note...

In the past, the problem of nighttime lighting in public housing was almost entirely kerosene lamps, which are also the most dangerous items that easily cause fires. In fact, in this city, electricity supply is cheap and convenient. If electric lights are fully installed, using these lower-wattage bulbs is about the same price as lighting kerosene lamps, and it can also reduce the risk of danger, which is the most economical. Therefore, the installation of electric lights seems to be a necessary facility in new public housing. The above are all fundamental solutions.

As for symptomatic fire prevention methods, that is, to prepare more emergency water pipes, and at the same time, measures should be taken to add fire extinguishers. As for the safety of doors and windows, special attention should also be paid to the design so that one can enter and exit freely in case of accidents.

(3) Recreation: The construction of public housing should preferably not be arranged as densely as beehives; within the scope possible, it is best to leave a part of the sunny open space. On this open space, several trees or a row of junipers can be planted. If economic conditions permit, it is possible to lay a layer of inferior lawn, which is not very expensive since the area is limited. This open space can allow civilians and their children to sit or rest at will, enjoy the sunshine, and make their lives more interesting.

The establishment of popular libraries is really urgent. When ordinary people are idle, due to lack of knowledge, they often indulge in bad habits such as gambling. Using the most space-saving way to set up a library, managed and guided by the more knowledgeable people in a dozen or so houses, to increase their knowledge at any time is the most wonderful way to promote popular education. The location of this kind of library can be at the center point of several houses.

The most economical building materials for houses are of course wood and bricks, etc., but the durability of wood is not good, so it is best to choose better wood. Thin plates can be used for the roof, and then a layer of tiles is laid on top. This construction method is indeed more economical.

The above-mentioned points are only the most important ones; there are many other small problems, but it is up to the architects to work hard.

Architectural Jargon (8)

— Mei Zhenhuan

——Regarding use on the construction site——

"Road Ghost" – The title "Road Ghost" is, apart from the "Boss," almost the most honorable on the construction site. But why is it called "Ghost"? This is probably because we Chinese have always called blue-eyed foreigners "foreign devils." He is a surveyor specially dispatched by the Construction Department or Public Works Bureau of the Municipal Council. His responsibility is to bear the responsibility for the safety of the entire building, and he has the supervisory position to ensure the safety of life. He also has the power to correct the errors in the academic guidance of the architect (i.e., the "pattern ghost"). Therefore, on the construction site, the "Road Ghost" is a tiger in the eyes of everyone, from the "pattern ghost" to the foremen.

Hand Mixed – What does "Hand Mixed" mean? It means work done by hand. Where is it used? It seems that ordinary building houses such as two-story city houses do not require a large amount of cement mixture, and there is no need to demand an increase in the production rate of the "roller," so people's hands are used to mix it.

Roller (Rounding Box) – A circular iron device with thin and strong iron plates forming inclined "partitions" in the middle. In use, a scaffolding is erected on top of the roller, paved with two-inch by twelve-inch foreign pine boards. A lead sheet is installed behind the roller, leading directly to the gap left on the foreign pine board. The cement, yellow sand, and stones are proportionally mixed and gradually poured down. The roller relies on electric power to rotate, and after three or four minutes, it is poured out at the central gap in the front, and it becomes a cooked mixture. (A cooked mixture is a well-mixed mixture.)

Small Cart – Shaped like a wheelbarrow, specially designed to transport things like cement mixtures.

Crane – If the number of floors of a building is six or seven stories high, it will be very difficult to transport the cement mixture that needs to be used. Relying solely on the transfer of the floating bridge (detailed above) is considered inappropriate in terms of time. In that case, the remedy is to use six-inch square foreign pine wood to build a frame, and then use a crane to lift the cement mixture up like an elevator with electric power. This kind of cart is called a crane, and it is shaped like a small boat with upturned ends.

Shell – For reinforced concrete projects, the initial equipment preparation is to follow the size, length, and width shown on the drawings. After calculating the positions according to the dimensions, two-inch by twelve-inch foreign pine boards are used to create a mold, regardless of beams, columns, stair steps, and so on. Then iron is tied. Once the iron is tied neatly, the cement mixture can be poured. This mold is called the shell (Formor Centerig).

Tying Iron – "Tying Iron" (Steel Elector) means that in the matched shell (regardless of beams, columns, stair steps, etc.), the steel bars are tied one by one with burnt lead wires. For example, ingot iron, bent iron, additional iron, straight iron, ring iron, and floor slab iron are all categories of names in tying iron.

Erecting Iron – Erecting foreign pine columns or cement column shell boards is called erecting iron.

Top Plate – The place where objects can be placed on the lower sill of a window is called the window sill, and the protruding one above the top sill is called the top plate (Toothing).

Lining – "Lining" (Lining) is the term for the "side posts" on both sides of a door or window. For more elaborate houses, lining boards (CliningBoard) are installed.

Scaffolding – A square frame made of old materials such as six-inch square, eight-inch square, ten-inch square, twelve-inch square, etc., prepared to place heavy materials on top for work.

Walings – When driving ordinary sheet piles, because of the severity of the depth, to prevent the sheet piles from being squeezed by external pressure, or there is a risk of collapse, a waling (Wiling) is added in advance around the sheet pile (SheetPile), approximately twelve inches square or ten inches square foreign pine wood, etc. (To be continued)

Perspective and Methods of Making Artificial Stone

— Chong

Artificial stone is also called terrazzo. It looks similar to marble from a distance. Its nature is also very hard, but not as hard as marble. Because this kind of artificial stone is made of water and stones of various colors, its texture is the same as that of cement, but with a few more polishing steps. After being rubbed on cement by a machine, it becomes very smooth and looks almost the same as marble. If it is used for floors in dance halls or large halls, it is very suitable, and it can be said to be economical and magnificent. Making this kind of floor can be said to be "once and for all," which can avoid the trouble of frequent repairs.

Artificial stone floors have the following excellent characteristics:

(1) You can choose the colors you like yourself, and they will never fade.

(2) Various patterns can be made.

(3) You can avoid the trouble of waxing.

(4) Its texture is harder and more beautiful than wooden floors.

(5) There is no need for frequent repairs or replacement. Its manufacturing method: (1) Use mountains and soil to make the bottom layer, about six inches high; (2) Mix cement, yellow sand, and stones (common stones), and then cover the mountain and soil with about three or four inches; (3) Mix cement and yellow sand, and then cover it on top, about two inches thick; (4) Cover with oil felt on the cement, and then use asphalt glue. This is to prevent underground moisture from rising; (5) Cover another layer of cement and yellow sand on top, about two inches thick; (6) Then use half-inch wide and two-tenths-inch thick copper strips, arranged vertically to form equal square shapes, or various patterns can be arranged. At the joints of the copper strips, use cement to glue them tightly; (7) Then mix cement with various colors and various colored stones (these colored stones are produced in Italy), and then carefully embed this colored cement, one by one, using whatever color you want. When all the embedding is completed, the first step of the cement worker's work is considered finished.

The second step is for the Shandong workers to polish the stones. They have a special machine for polishing stones. The machine has a motor and a turntable below. On this turntable, there are three stones for polishing, and the thickness of these three stones can be changed at will. When the motor is turned on, the turntable rotates, so the three stones below also rub against the ground.

The procedure for polishing stones takes three times in total. The first time is one week later. They use the coarsest stone for polishing and install it on the turntable. When the motor is turned on, it rubs against the ground. This time of polishing is the longest, because it is necessary to polish off the layer of unclean cement on top before you can see the colors below and the beautiful colored stones, as well as the two-tenths-inch thick golden copper strips, which are also revealed on top. At that time, grids of various colors and golden edges can already be seen, but they are not very smooth. The stones used for the second polishing are finer than the first time, and the polishing time is also shorter. Next is the third polishing, which is to replace it with a finest stone for polishing, and also sprinkle a very fine snow-white powder (the name of the powder is unknown, it is said to contain toxic substances) on the ground, and then use the machine to polish it. It is said that this powder can make the stone shine brightly and become smooth, and it can also make the colors bright and beautiful.

Study of Building Materials (9)

— Zhu Zhenmu

(4) Adding Copper – If 1% to 2% of copper is added to steel during refining, it can block electrical erosion and prevent rust. Chromium also has this effect. Stainless steel on the market contains this substance.

(5) Polishing – Because the unevenness of the surface of the steel plate can create its own positive and negative electrodes, it is easy to rust. If it is polished, this problem can be eliminated.

Section 3: Welding Methods

The connection methods for the application of steel and iron include riveting and nailing, which are common. Another welding method deserves to be briefly described here.

There are two types of force welding: force welding and fusion welding:

Force Welding – Force welding is the method of heating the two ends of an iron plate slightly to soften them and then striking them with force to make them connect.

Fusion Welding – Welding is the method of heating the two ends of an iron plate together to melt them and then sticking them together. When it cools, they are already merged and welded together. The heating method is divided into three categories:

(1) Blowpipe Method – Using a mixed gas of Acetglene and oxygen, which is blown out through a blowpipe and ignited, can obtain a high temperature of 1800 degrees Fahrenheit, which is sufficient to melt and weld steel. This method is convenient for emergency repairs and is widely used.

(2) Reduction Method – A mixture of iron dioxide and aluminum is heated red to 4000 degrees Fahrenheit to obtain molten iron, which can be poured onto the joint to weld it. This method is mostly used for repairing cracks.

(3) Electric Welding Method – Using alternating or direct current, and discharging electricity with two electrodes at a distance, can melt and weld steel. This method is mostly used in the manufacture of steel products. (End of Chapter 5)
